‡§Ö‡§• ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡•§

‘‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à’ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π- ‘‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§®‡•ç’ ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§£‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‘‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§µ’ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‘‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§®‡•ç’ ‡•• ‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He lays down the third layer. For the gods, having laid down the second layer, now ascended it; but, indeed, they thereby completed and ascended to what is above the earth and below the atmosphere.

‡§§‡•á ‡§Ω‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç- ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø, ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ ‡§§‡§¶‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç- ‡§á‡§§ ‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•® ‡••

‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§£‡•á ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‘‡§§‡•á’ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‘‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡•§ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§§‡•á- ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ ‡§§‡§¶‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á’ ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç’ ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∑‡§ü‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ (‡§∂. ‡§™. ‡•Æ ‡•§ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•Æ) ‡•§ ‘‡§è‡§∑‡§É’ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§õ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•Ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•® ‡••

Eggeling
  1. They spate, ‘Meditate ye!’ whereby, indeed, they meant to say, ‘Seek ye a layer! Seek ye (to build) upwards from hence!’ Whilst meditating, they saw the great third layer, even the air: that world pleased them.

Eggeling
  1. They said to Indra and Agni, ‘Lay ye down for us this third layer!’–‘What will accrue unto us therefrom? Ye two shall be the best of us!’–‘So be it!’ Accordingly Indra and Agni laid down for them that third layer; and hence people say, ‘Indra and Agni are the best of gods.’

  1. He accordingly lays it down by means of Indra and Agni, and settles it by means of Vi≈õvakarman 2,

‘‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§™‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Ñ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‘‡§Ö‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç’ ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ? ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á- ‡§â‡§™ ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Æ‡§æ’ ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§§’ ‡§â‡§™‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§ ‡§â‡§™‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‘‡§Æ‡•á’ ‡§Æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§’ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Æ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§™‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡•à‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§§‡§•‡•á‡§§‡§ø’ ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‘‡§§‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç’ ‡§ö‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ß‡•Å‡§É’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡•• ‡•¨ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He said to them, ‘Come ye to me and restore ye to me wherewith ye are going from me!’–‘What will accrue unto us therefrom?’–‘That (part) of my body shall be sacred unto you!’–‘So be it!’ So Indra and Agni, and Vi≈õvakarman restored that (part) unto him.

Eggeling
  1. Now that central Svayam-ƒÅtrÃ•·πá·πáƒÅ (naturally-perforated brick) 4 is that very (part) of his body;–when he now lays down that (brick), he thereby restores to him that (part) of his (PrajƒÅpati’s) body which this (brick represents): this is why he now lays down that (brick).

“‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Ω‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ÉÍ£≥‡§π‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡•§ “‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Ω‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡§æ‡§ß‡§∏‡•á”- (‡§µ‡§æ‡•¶ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡•¶ ‡•ß‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•ß) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Ω‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡§æ‡§ß‡§§‡•á ‡•• ‡•Æ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π- ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡•§ ‘‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§É’ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§∞‡•ã ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§∂‡§É ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‘‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä’ ‘‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡§≤‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ç’ ‘‡§¶‡•É‡§Ç‡§π‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§¶‡•É‡§¢‡•Ä‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡•á ! ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‘‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á‡§®’ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‘‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ö’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§¨‡§æ‡§ß‡§∏‡•á’ ‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á- ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§π‡§ø’ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ’ ‡§∏‡§ï‡§≤‡§ú‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‘‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§Ö‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø “‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•Å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ? ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á’ ‡§è‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç, ‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö ‘‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§µ‡§§‡•ç, ‘‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç’ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ”- ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§É, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•à‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡•• ‡•Æ-‡•Ø ‡••

Eggeling
  1. [VƒÅj. S. XIV, 11], ‘O Indra and Agni, make ye fast the brick so as not to shake!’ as the text so the sense;–‘with thy back thou forcest asunder the earth, and the sky, and the air;’ for with its back this (brick) indeed forces asunder the earth, and the sky, and the air.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

“‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•Å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‚Äú‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§Ç‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•Ä‡§É"- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ, ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§Ç‡§π, ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•Ä‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•Ø ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. [VƒÅj. S. XIV, 12], ‘May Vi≈õvakarman settle

thee,’ for Vi≈õvakarman saw this third layer;–‘on the back of the air, thee the wide, the broad one!’ for this (brick) indeed is the wide and broad back of the air;–‘support thou the air, make fast the air, injure not the air!’ that is, ‘support thou thine own self (body), make fast thine own self, injure not thine own self!’

‡•ß‡•¶

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò) ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡••

‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‘‡§õ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ’ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç (‡§®‡§ø‡§ò‡§Ç. ‡•© ‡•§ ‡•™ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•Æ ‡•§) ‘‡§§‡•á‡§®’ ‡§ö ‘‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ’ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•Å’ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ “‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ “‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§¶‡§¶‡•ã‡§π‡§∏‡§É‚Äù- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç (‡•≠ ‡•§ ‡•ß ‡•§ ‡•ß ‡•§ ‡•®‡•¨) ‡§Ö‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø-‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§•’ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ’ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§â‡§™‡§∞‡§ø’ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•¶ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. ‘For all up-breathing, and dawn-breathing, and through-breathing, and out-breathing!’ for the naturally-perforated (brick) is the vital air, and the vital air serves for everything here;–‘for a resting-place and moving-place!’ for the naturally-perforated (brick) is these worlds, and these worlds are indeed a resting-place and a moving-place;–‘May VƒÅyu shelter thee!’ that is, ‘May VƒÅyu protect thee!’–‘with grand prosperity!’ that is, ‘with great prosperity;’–‘with most auspicious protection!’–that is, with what protection is most auspicious.’ Having settled it 5, he pronounces the S≈´dadohas 6 over it; the meaning of this has been explained. He then sings a sƒÅman: the meaning of this (will be explained) further on 7.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ-‡§§‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ-‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§É‡§∏‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§ü‡§≠‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ-‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ã‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ-‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡•ß‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He then lays down (five) Di≈õyƒÅ (regional bricks) 9. Now the regional ones, doubtless, are

the regions: it is the regions he thus bestows (on the air-world). And these are those same regions not separated (from the air) wherewith VƒÅyu on that occasion 10 stepped nigh: it is them he thereby bestows. But prior to these same (bricks) he lays down 11 both the bunch of Darbha grass and the clod-bricks; and these (di≈õyƒÅs) being yonder sun 12, he thus places yonder sun over the regions, and builds him up upon (or, in) the regions. But were these (laid down) at the same time (as the bunch of grass and the clod-bricks), they would be outside (of the altar); and outside of the womb (foundation), indeed, is that sacrificial work regarding the fire-altar which is done prior to the lotus-leaf 13. When he

now brings and lays down these (bricks), he thereby establishes them in the womb, on the lotus-leaf, and thus these (bricks) are not outside (the fire-altar). He lays them down so as not to be separated 14 from the naturally-perforated one; for the middle 15 naturally-perforated one is the air: he thus places the regions so as not to be separate from the air. Subsequently 16 (to the central brick he lays them down): subsequently to the air he thus sets up the regions. In all (four) directions he places them: he thus places the regions (quarters) in all directions, whence the regions are in all (four) directions. [He places them] on all sides so as to face each other: he thereby makes the regions on all sides face each other, and hence the regions on all sides face each other 17.

‡•ß‡•®

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he lays down the regionals. The regions, doubtless, are the metres–the eastern region being the GƒÅyatrƒ´, the southern the Trish·π≠ubh, the western the Jagatƒ´, the northern the Anush·π≠ubh, and the upper region the Pa·πÖkti;–and the metres are animals 18, and the middlemost layer is the air: he thus places animals in the air,

and hence there are animals that have their abode in the air 19.

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§µ‡•ã) ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§â‡§™‡§¶·≥ò‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§É ‡•§ ‡§™‡§∂‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡§µ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ | ‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§É‡§∏‡§ø‡§ö‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§Ø‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§É‡§∏‡§ø‡§ö‡•å ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å ‡§™‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§ ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•ß‡•© ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‘‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡§µ‡§É’ ‡§â‡§™‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É ‡•§ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§á‡§π ‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•© ‡••

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he lays down the regionals. The regions, doubtless, are the metres, and the metres are animals, and animals are food, and the middlemost layer is the middle: he thus puts food in the middle (of the body). He places them so as not to be separated (by special bricks) from the naturally-perforated one; for the naturally-perforated one is the vital air: he thus places the food so as not to be separated from the vital air. Subsequently (to the central brick he lays them down): subsequently to (or upon) the vital air he thus places food. On the range of the Reta·∏•sic (he places them): the Reta·∏•sic being the ribs, and the ribs being the middle (of the body), he thus places the food in the middle of this (Agni’s body). On every side he places them: from everywhere he thus supplies him with food.

“‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø” ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‘‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø’ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‘‡§∏‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•Ä,’ ‘‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§°‡•ç’- ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‘‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø’ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§£ ‘‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç’ ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§® “‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø”- ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§µ ‘‡§è‡§®‡§æ‡§É’ ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡•á ! ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‘‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•Ä’ ‡§è‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ ? ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§â‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç; ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç; ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•™ ‡••

‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•á ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∂‡§§‡§™‡§•‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•á ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• (‡•Æ-‡•©-‡•ß) ‡••

‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§ï‡§É ‡•• ‡•Æ ‡•§ ‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. [He lays them down, with, VƒÅj. S. XIV, 13], ‘Thou art the queen, the Eastern region! Thou art the far-ruler, the Southern region! Thou art the all-ruler, the Western region! Thou art the self-ruler, the Northern region! Thou art the supreme ruler, the Great region!’ these are their names: he thus lays them down whilst naming them. Separately he lays them down, separately he settles them, and separately he pronounces the S≈´dadohas over them, for separate are the regions.

  2. 41:4 For the connection of these deities with the third layer, and the air, see also VI, 2, 3, 3. Vi≈õvakarman is likewise the deity by which the Vi≈õvajyotis-brick, representing VƒÅyu (the wind), the regent of the air-world, is settled; see VIII, 3, 2, 3. ↩︎

  3. ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§æ. ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•å. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•ß‡•≠ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•Ø‡•ß ‡•§ ↩︎

  4. 42:1 See part iii, p. 155, note 8. ↩︎

  5. 43:1 Viz. by the concluding formula, ‘With the help of that deity, A·πÖgiras-like, lie thou steady!’ see part iii, p. 302, note 3. ↩︎

  6. 43:2 Viz. VƒÅj. S. XII, 55 (RÃ•g-veda S. VIII, 69, 3), ‘At his birth the well-like milking, speckled ones mix the Soma, the clans of the gods in the three spheres of the heavens.’ See part iii, p. 307, note 2. ↩︎

  7. 43:3 VIII, 7, 4, 1 seq. ↩︎

  8. ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Ç‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§É‡§∏‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§™‡§Ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ. ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•å. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•ß‡•≠ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•Ø‡•® ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§É ‡•§ ↩︎

  9. 43:4 The five Di≈õyƒÅs are placed on the spines in the four directions at the reta·∏•sic range, just over where the five Vai≈õvadevƒ´ bricks were placed in the second layer (see the sketch, p. 24). Between them and the central (naturally-perforated) brick there is thus an empty space a foot square, and the two southern Di≈õyƒÅs are half-bricks lying north and south of each other. ↩︎

  10. 44:1 See VI, 2, 3, 4. The second naturally-perforated brick represents the air-world with which VƒÅyu, the wind, is most closely associated. ↩︎

  11. 44:2 That is to say, he laid them down on the site of the altar, before the first layer was commenced, viz. the darbha-bunch in the centre of the ‘body’ of the altar, where the two spines (an≈´ka) intersect each other (VII, 2, 3, 1 seqq.); and the clod-bricks (logesh·π≠akƒÅ) on the four ends of the two spines (VII, 3, 1, 23 seqq.), that is, in the middle of each of the four sides of the square of which the body’ consists. ↩︎

  12. 44:3 The symbolic interpretation here seems somewhat confused, inasmuch as the Di≈õyƒÅs, which are now apparently identified with the sun, have just been stated to represent the regions. At VI, 7, 1, 17 the sun was represented as the central point of the universe to which these three worlds are linked by means of the quarters (as by the strings of a scale). The clod-bricks, on the other hand, were indeed, in VII, 3, I, 13, identified with the regions (quarters); and the bunch of grass, being laid down in the centre, might be regarded as marking the fifth region, that upwards from here. Cf. IX, 5, 1, 36. ↩︎

  13. 44:4 The lotus-leaf is placed in the centre of the altar when the first layer is about to be laid down. See VII, 4, 1, 7 seqq., where it is explained as representing the foundation of the fire-altar, or rather, the womb whence Agni is born. ↩︎

  14. 45:1 That is, not separated therefrom by other special bricks; though the full space of one brick is left between the Di≈õyƒÅs and the central brick. Perhaps, however, ‘anantarhita’ here means ‘immediately after.’ ↩︎

  15. 45:2 That is, the second of the three svayam-ƒÅtrÃ•·πá·πáƒÅs, the one in the third layer. ↩︎

  16. 45:3 Uttara seems here and elsewhere to have a double meaning, viz. that of subsequent, and upper, or left, inasmuch as looking towards these bricks from the centre of the altar, they are placed to the left of the particular section of the an≈´kas. ↩︎

  17. 45:4 See p. 26, note 3. ↩︎

  18. 45:5 The metres are commonly represented as cattle. ↩︎

  19. 46:1 That is all (four-footed) animals that dwell on, not in, the earth. The GƒÅyatrƒ´ metre, at any rate, is also represented as a bird which fetches the Soma from heaven, but it is not the air as such that is intended here, but the face of the earth. ↩︎
